",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Once a suggestion arrives, how should that change be presented inside a live editor?"}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Pochiâ€™s NES is built as a VS Code-native feature, not a standalone IDE or a custom fork. The editor is a continuously changing environment and does not function like a static canvas. Sometimes the user's cursor might be exactly where the edit belongs, or it can be twenty lines away, or the suggestion itself can be a huge change spanning multiple lines."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Showing such suggestions naÃ¯vely introduces new failure modes that are easy to trigger and hard to ignore. One experiences jumps in cursor position, abrupt viewport scrolls, or rendering large changes directly in the editing flow. In practice, these behaviors are often more disruptive than not showing a suggestion at all."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["This brings us to the most fundamental design question: ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"How do we show an edit without stealing the developerâ€™s attention?"}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Answering that question requires understanding the VS Code interaction model."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"VS Code does not provide a built-in API for previewing LLM-generated edits. Instead, the editor offers different primitives for different kinds of locations and edits. These primitives are optimized for various interaction patterns, each with their own affordances and limitations. Some work well for cursor-local edits, while others are better suited for changes elsewhere in the file."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Understanding this difference is key. Pochi's NES does not render suggestions in a single, fixed way. Instead, NES relies on these primitives to create a balance between visibility and disruption."}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"dynamic-rendering-strategy","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#dynamic-rendering-strategy","className":"peer","children":"Dynamic Rendering Strategy"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Rather than forcing all suggestions into a single representation, we designed a Dynamic Rendering Strategy offering the optimal visual experiences in different editing scenarios:"}],"\n",["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["Suggestions that target ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"the current cursor position"}]," are rendered inline, flowing naturally into the user's typing behavior."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["Suggestions that apply ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"off-cursor"}]," are previewed via an inline diff decoration, avoiding jumps in the viewport."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["For ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"large, multi-line block inserts"}],", a floating preview is used to provide sufficient context without disrupting the user's current focus."]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"This way, each path is deliberately scoped to the situations where it performs best, aligning it with the least disruptive representation for a given edit."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Letâ€™s take a walk-through of these rendering strategies in detail and examine when each one is used, starting with the least disruptive case."}],"\n",["$","h3",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"inline-completion","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#inline-completion","className":"peer","children":"Inline Completion"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"When an edit is positioned right at the cursor, the least disruptive option is to stay out of the way. In such cases, we render the edit inline, making it blend directly into the user's typing flow."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"To achieve this, we use VS Code's inline completion API. This approach works especially well for small, localized changes like autoclosing brackets, replacing a few characters, or edits that are directly made under the cursor."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"NES Cover Image Part 4","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/nes-inline-completion-blog.a236fa9f.gif","height":1080,"width":2896,"blurWidth":0,"blurHeight":0},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","h3",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"inline-diff-preview","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#inline-diff-preview","className":"peer","children":"Inline Diff Preview"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Because NES predicts the next meaningful edit across the file (not just at the cursor), many suggestions naturally apply outside the userâ€™s current editing position. For example, while you are typing inside a function, NES may suggest updating a related import, adjusting a type definition, or fixing a reference several lines away."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"In these cases, the cost of getting the presentation wrong is high. The user is forced to jump across the file, break context and interrupt their flow."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"To avoid that, we render the suggestion as an inline diff decoration. The text to be replaced is highlighted in red, while the new content is shown in green at the insertion point. This way, the user gets a clear preview of the change without moving the cursor."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"NES Cover Image Part 4","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/inline-diff-completion-nes-part-4-blog.cdd15366.gif","height":1080,"width":2896,"blurWidth":0,"blurHeight":0},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"This works particularly well for changes involving single-line updates or even multiple lines where each line is being changed independently."}],"\n",["$","h3",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"floating-diff-image","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#floating-diff-image","className":"peer","children":"Floating Diff Image"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Because NES has the ability to propose structural edits, such as inserting a new helper function, refactoring a block of logic, or adding a multi-line configuration, it frequently produces multi-line suggestions that cannot be represented as simple, inline changes."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"In these cases, the suggestion is no longer tied to the cursorâ€™s immediate context, and the standard inline rendering stratergies do not suffice."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"At this point, the decision falls under either pulling the user away from where theyâ€™re working or bringing the preview to them. Since preserving developer flow is a core design principle for NES, we consistently choose the latter."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"In order to make the suggestion appear near the edit target without moving the cursor, we generate a floating diff preview and render it as an image. The color schema of the suggestion will also stay consistent with the other solutions we discussed previously - red for deleted text, and green for inserted ones."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"VS Code allows extensions to attach image-based decorations. With careful layout and positioning, these decorations can be floated near the edit target and used as a diff preview. However, the editor does not render code into images, which means the preview has to be generated by the extension itself."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"This required a small rendering pipeline:"}],"\n",["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Theme matching:"}]," Every VS Code theme is an extension with a standard JSON format. We parse the active theme, extract its token colour map, and match it to the userâ€™s active settings so the preview matches the theme in the editor."]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Syntax highlighting:"}]," VSCode includes a bundled ",["$","code",null,{"children":"TextMate"}]," runtime. We load the grammar for the current filetype, generate syntax scopes, and apply the same colouring rules that VS Code uses. This ensures that the rendered code maintains the same appearance as the code in the editor."]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Image rendering:"}]," Here we use ",["$","code",null,{"children":"canvaskit-wasm"}]," to render the tokenized code into an image. it is RL that is necessary to teach them what works. On the other hand, introducing RL in software engineering brings its own specific challenges:  data availability, signal sparsity, and state tracking. In this post, weâ€™ll break down how recent works address these challenges."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"Reinforcement Learning is Changing AI Coding Cover Image","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/rl-blog-cover-image.ac318676.png","height":1288,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAAECAMAAACEE47CAAAAElBMVEUmLTE2QkQkJyYwMSwuNDk7SlI5s3xfAAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAIklEQVR4nBXGtw0AAAzDMLn9/3KQhSA2lFeb1EC1ToFvnAMEqgBFxbZJ4gAAAABJRU5ErkJggg==","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":4},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"So far, the focus of RL driven improvements had been based on competitive coding. For example, in LeetCode-style tasks, the model works in a closed loop. It generally receives a clear problem statement and in turn, it generates a single, self-contained solution."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"This means there are no dependencies involved, no files systems to navigate, and no legacy code that can break. It is exactly like solving a logic puzzle in isolation rather than understanding the engineering implications on the overall codebase."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"However, the field of Software Engineering (SWE) in real-world is fundamentally different. It is a stateful, multi-turn interactive problem. A day-to-day involves much more than just writing the correct functions. You often need to navigate a file system, check up on dependency graphs, run the proper tests, and interpret logs in case of errors. This implies, an agent effectively needs to maintain coherence across a long horizon of interactions."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Which is why RL is an ideal candidate for SWE since agent actions produce verifiable results. At the same time, it also introduces challenges that are not present in single-turn tasks. For example,"}],"\n",["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Data Availability:"}]," We cannot easily simulate millions of environmental interactions like we can with math problems."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Signal Sparsity:"}]," Often, success signals appear at the very end of a long sequence of edits."]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"State Tracking:"}]," Along with the static text of the code, the model must understand the dynamic state of the runtime environment"]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Recent works from Meta and Moonshot AI surfaced how the industry is pivoting from general reasoning RL to domain-specific SWE-RL to address these challenges."}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"the-data-problem","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#the-data-problem","className":"peer","children":"The Data Problem"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"In order to learn trial and error, the standard RL requires an agent to interact with an environment. For coding, this means running a test suite or compiling code. As compared to verifying math proof, this simulation will be prohibitively slow and expensive in a real-world setting. Here, the engineering challenges arises to figure out how to bootstrap the entire learning process without being dependent on costly online simulation."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["Meta proved that you can bypass the online bottleneck by using the massive offline history of Github. In its recent work on ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"SWE-RL"}]," they talked through this approach instead of setting up a live sandbox for every training step."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"But offline data lacks a reward signal. For every historical Pull Request, you cannot easily go back in time and execute tests. SWE-RL solves this by creating a process proxy reward. They calculate the fine grained text similarity  between the generated patch and the actual developer ground truth solution instead of just checking if the code runs."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"Process proxy reward","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/swe-process-proxy-reward.69e3750b.png","height":1500,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAAFCAMAAABPT11nAAAABlBMVEUqJyM0LyjG/bGAAAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAG0lEQVR4nGNgZGRgYAATIAChGRmhAsgMBgYGAAGOABE3/Z+DAAAAAElFTkSuQmCC","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":5},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Depending on how closely the generated format matches the human solution, the model receives a continuous reward. On the other hand, if the model generates an invalid patch format, it receives a penalty. This demonstrates that even before touching a compiler, you can teach a model complex engineering behaviours like navigating file structures and adhering to project conventions using static history."}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"the-signal-sparsity-problem","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#the-signal-sparsity-problem","className":"peer","children":"The Signal Sparsity Problem"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Next, we have the credit assignment problem while facing online training within executable environments. That means it is difficult to indentify which step really contributed to the final success of the model and which step should get the reward. This reflects on software engineering as any agent can fail after 50 steps of editing and testing. Standard RL struggles to identify which specific step caused the failure."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["The ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Kimi-Dev"}]," paper addresses this through task decomposition. It treats software engineering as a composition of atomic skills: the BugFixer (editing logic) and the TestWriter (verifying logic) instead of training an end-to-end agent to solve the issue immediately."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Their solution starts with Agentless RL. They train the model specifically on these short horizon atomic tasks using outcome based rewards. They look for signals on whether the patch passed the test or did the test reproduce the bug. And since the tasks are scoped down, the feedback signal becomes dense and clear."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Kimi-Dev shows that with minimal additional data, a model having these pre-trained capabilities can be adapted to a complex multi-turn agent framework. This suggests that the most efficient path to autonomous agents is rigorous skill acquisitionâ€™s followed by workflow adaptation rather than brute force end to end training."}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"the-state-problem-building-a-code-world-model","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#the-state-problem-building-a-code-world-model","className":"peer","children":"The State Problem: Building a Code World Model"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Coming to the final challenge, which is also arguably the most profound. Engineers generally do not just read code as text but also think about the execution loops in their mind. This involves tracking how variables change in memory and how functions interact between files. Meanwhile, since current code LLMs lack this internal compiler engine, they just merely predict the next token based on statistical likelihood."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["Meta ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Code World Model"}]," addresses this by fundamentally changing the training curriculum. They realized that waiting until the RL phase to teach execution dynamics is too late. The rewards are too sparse and the gradient vanishes on hard problems."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Instead, in the mid-training stage, they inject process supervision directly. To teach the physics of code, they constructed two massive datasets:"}],"\n",["$","ul",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"Python Execution Traces:"}]," With over 120 million examples, the model is trained to predict not just the next line of code, but also the exact state of runtime variables (the values in memory) after every single line."]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":["\n",["$","p",null,{"children":[["$","strong",null,{"children":"ForagerAgent Trajectories:"}]," Agents with 3 million trajectories that interact with a Docker environment to solve tasks."]}],"\n"]}],"\n"]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"This forces the model to internalise a Code World Model. By the time the model enters the final RL stage it is no longer starting from scratch. It already understands if I write X then variable Y changes to Z."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"Consequently, the RL stage becomes a process of Goal Alignment. It uses sparse result rewards like passing tests simply to guide a model.  It already understands execution physics to select the specific path that satisfies the verification requirement."}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["$","$La",null,{"alt":"Goal Alignment","placeholder":"blur","src":{"src":"/_next/static/media/goal-alignment.bd10f8a2.png","height":1011,"width":2358,"blurDataURL":"data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAgAAAADCAMAAACZFr56AAAABlBMVEUuKiY0MSxBDjzTAAAACXBIWXMAACE4AAAhOAFFljFgAAAAFElEQVR4nGNgYGSAAiQGIyMDIwMAAFYABxixu7cAAAAASUVORK5CYII=","blurWidth":8,"blurHeight":3},"basePath":""}]}],"\n",["$","h2",null,{"className":"flex scroll-m-28 flex-row items-center gap-2","id":"takeaway-moving-toward-verifiable-agents","children":[["$","a",null,{"data-card":"","href":"#takeaway-moving-toward-verifiable-agents","className":"peer","children":"Takeaway: Moving Toward Verifiable Agents"}],["$","svg",null,{"ref":"$undefined","xmlns":"http://www.w3.org/2000/svg","width":24,"height":24,"viewBox":"0 0 24 24","fill":"none","stroke":"currentColor","strokeWidth":2,"strokeLinecap":"round","strokeLinejoin":"round","className":"lucide size-3.5 shrink-0 text-fd-muted-foreground opacity-0 transition-opacity peer-hover:opacity-100","aria-label":"Link to section","children":[[["$","path","1cjeqo",{"d":"M10 13a5 5 0 0 0 7.54.54l3-3a5 5 0 0 0-7.07-7.07l-1.72 1.71"}],["$","path","19qd67",{"d":"M14 11a5 5 0 0 0-7.54-.54l-3 3a5 5 0 0 0 7.07 7.07l1.71-1.71"}]],"$undefined"]}]]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":["This progression from ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"SWE-RL (offline proxy rewards)"}]," to ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"Kimi-Dev (decomposed skill learning)"}]," and ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"CWM (execution-trace world models)"}]," outlines a clear engineering roadmap for the next generation of code models and agentic RL frameworks."]}],"\n",["$","p",null,{"children":"We are seeing a shift from generic reasoning to specialized engineering.
